(14,808\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n        <th>\n         Max length\n        </th>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n        <th>\n         Power consumption\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         2000\xe2\x80\x932500\xc2\xa0W\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n        <th>\n         Min altitude\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         341\xc2\xa0km (184 nmi)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n        <th>\n         Max altitude\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         353\xc2\xa0km (191 nmi)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n        <th>\n         Period\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         ~91 minutes\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer\n       </b>\n       , also designated\n       <b>\n        AMS-02\n       </b>\n       , is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">\n        particle physics\n       </a>\n       experiment module that is mounted on the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS). The module is a detector that measures\n       <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">\n        antimatter\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">\n        cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       , this information is needed to understand the formation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">\n        Universe\n       </a>\n       and search for evidence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">\n        dark matter\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Principal_investigator" title="Principal investigator">\n        principal investigator\n       </a>\n       is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_laureate" title="Nobel laureate">\n        Nobel laureate\n       </a>\n       particle physicist\n       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_C._C._Ting" title="Samuel C. C. Ting">\n        Samuel Ting\n       </a>\n       . The launch of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       flight\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n        STS-134\n       </a>\n       carrying AMS-02 took place on 16 May 2011, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spectrometer" title="Spectrometer">\n        spectrometer\n       </a>\n       was installed on 19 May 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESTEC2_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESTEC2-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By April 15, 2015, AMS-02 had recorded over 60 billion cosmic ray events\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMS02_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AMS02-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and 90 billion after five years of operation since its installation in May 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMS02-2016_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AMS02-2016-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In March 2013, at a seminar at CERN, Professor Samuel Ting reported that AMS had observed over 400,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       , with the positron to electron fraction increasing from 10 GeV to 250 GeV. (Later results have shown a decrease in positron fraction at energies over about 275 GeV). There was "no significant variation over time, or any preferred incoming direction. These results are consistent with the positrons originating from the annihilation of dark matter particles in space, but not yet sufficiently conclusive to rule out other explanations." The results have been published in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Physical_Review_Letters" title="Physical Review Letters">\n         Physical Review Letters\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physrevltrs413_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-physrevltrs413-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additional data are still being collected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physrevltrs413_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-physrevltrs413-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMS-20130403_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AMS-20130403-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20130403_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20130403-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-20130403_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-20130403-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20130403_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20130403-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130403_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130403-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n           </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a href="#Installation_on_the_International_Space_Station">\n <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The alpha magnetic spectrometer was proposed in 1995 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">\n        MIT\n       </a>\n       particle physicist Samuel Ting, not long after the cancellation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Superconducting_Super_Collider" title="Superconducting Super Collider">\n        Superconducting Super Collider\n       </a>\n       . The proposal was accepted and Ting became the\n       <a href="/wiki/Principal_investigator" title="Principal investigator">\n        principal investigator\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="AMS-01">\n        AMS-01\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: AMS-01">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:425px;max-width:425px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:145px;max-width:145px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-91_PLB.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1451" data-file-width="1035" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/STS-91_PLB.jpg/143px-STS-91_PLB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/STS-91_PLB.jpg/215px-STS-91_PLB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/STS-91_PLB.jpg/286px-STS-91_PLB.jpg 2x" width="143"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          AMS-01 flew in space in June 1998 aboard the\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n           Space Shuttle\n           <i>\n            Discovery\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          on\n          <a href="/wiki/STS-91" title="STS-91">\n           STS-91\n          </a>\n          . It is visible near the rear of the payload bay.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:276px;max-width:276px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-91_AMS-01_Detail.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="171" data-file-width="234" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cb/STS-91_AMS-01_Detail.jpg" width="274"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          A detail view of the AMS-01 module (center) mounted in the\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n           shuttle\n          </a>\n          payload bay for the\n          <a href="/wiki/STS-91" title="STS-91">\n           STS-91\n          </a>\n          mission.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       An AMS prototype designated AMS-01, a simplified version of the detector, was built by the international consortium under Ting\'s direction and flown into space aboard the\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-91" title="STS-91">\n        STS-91\n       </a>\n       in June 1998. By not detecting any\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antihelium#Antihelium" title="Antihelium">\n        antihelium\n       </a>\n       the\n       <i>\n        AMS-01\n       </i>\n       established an upper limit of 1.1\xc3\x9710\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x926\n       </sup>\n       for the antihelium to helium\n       <a href="/wiki/Flux" title="Flux">\n        flux\n       </a>\n       ratio\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and proved that the detector concept worked in space. This shuttle mission was the last shuttle flight to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n        <i>\n         Mir\n        </i>\n        Space Station\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="AMS-02">\n        AMS-02\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: AMS-02">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AMS01Geneva.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/AMS01Geneva.jpg/220px-AMS01Geneva.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/AMS01Geneva.jpg/330px-AMS01Geneva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/AMS01Geneva.jpg/440px-AMS01Geneva.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AMS01Geneva.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         AMS-02 during integration and testing at\n         <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">\n          CERN\n         </a>\n         near Geneva.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After the flight of the prototype, Ting began the development of a full research system designated AMS-02. This development effort involved the work of 500 scientists from 56 institutions and 16 countries organized under\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">\n        United States Department of Energy\n       </a>\n       (DOE) sponsorship.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The instrument which eventually resulted from a long evolutionary process has been called "the most sophisticated particle detector ever sent into space", rivaling very large detectors used at major\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">\n        particle accelerators\n       </a>\n       , and has cost four times as much as any of its ground-based counterparts. Its goals have also evolved and been refined over time. As it is built as a more comprehensive detector, which has a better chance of discovering evidence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">\n        dark matter\n       </a>\n       along other goals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The power requirements for AMS-02 were thought to be too great for a practical independent spacecraft. So AMS-02 was designed to be installed as an external module on the International Space Station and use power from the ISS. The post-\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       plan was to deliver AMS-02 to the ISS by space shuttle in 2005 on\n       <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_International_Space_Station" title="Assembly of the International Space Station">\n        station assembly\n       </a>\n       mission\n       <b>\n        UF4.1\n       </b>\n       , but technical difficulties and shuttle scheduling issues added more delays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-overview-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       AMS-02 successfully completed final integration and operational testing at\n       <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">\n        CERN\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneva,_Switzerland" title="Geneva, Switzerland">\n        Geneva, Switzerland\n       </a>\n       which included exposure to energetic\n       <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">\n        proton\n       </a>\n       beams generated by the CERN\n       <a href="/wiki/Super_Proton_Synchrotron" title="Super Proton Synchrotron">\n        SPS particle accelerator\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       AMS-02 was then shipped by\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.route-to-space.eu/index.php/en/projects/alpha-magnetic-spectrometer" rel="nofollow">\n        specialist haulier\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        ESA\'s\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Research_and_Technology_Centre" title="European Space Research and Technology Centre">\n        European Space Research and Technology Centre\n       </a>\n       (ESTEC) facility in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">\n        Netherlands\n       </a>\n       where it arrived 16 February 2010. Here it underwent thermal vacuum,\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_compatibility" title="Electromagnetic compatibility">\n        electromagnetic compatibility\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_interference" title="Electromagnetic interference">\n        electromagnetic interference\n       </a>\n       testing. AMS-02 was scheduled for delivery to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       , United States. in late May 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESTEC2_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESTEC2-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was however postponed to August 26, as AMS-02 underwent final alignment beam testing at CERN.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amsliftedatgva_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-amsliftedatgva-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESTEC_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESTEC-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amsbeamtesting.JPG">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Amsbeamtesting.JPG/200px-Amsbeamtesting.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Amsbeamtesting.JPG/300px-Amsbeamtesting.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Amsbeamtesting.JPG/400px-Amsbeamtesting.JPG 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          AMS-02 during final alignment testing at\n          <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">\n           CERN\n          </a>\n          just days before being airlifted to\n          <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n           Cape Canaveral\n          </a>\n          .\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beamfeedingams.JPG">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Beamfeedingams.JPG/200px-Beamfeedingams.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Beamfeedingams.JPG/300px-Beamfeedingams.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Beamfeedingams.JPG/400px-Beamfeedingams.JPG 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Beamline from\n          <a href="/wiki/Super_Proton_Synchrotron" title="Super Proton Synchrotron">\n           SPS\n          </a>\n          feeding 20 GeV\n          <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n           positrons\n          </a>\n          to AMS for alignment testing at the time of the picture.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A cryogenic,\n       <a href="/wiki/Superconducting_magnet" title="Superconducting magnet">\n        superconducting magnet\n       </a>\n       system was developed for the AMS-02. With\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obama_administration" title="Obama administration">\n        Obama administration\n       </a>\n       plans to extend International Space Station operations beyond 2015, the decision was made by AMS management to exchange the AMS-02 superconducting magnet for the non-superconducting magnet previously flown on AMS-01. Although the non-superconducting magnet has a weaker\n       <a href="/wiki/Field_strength" title="Field strength">\n        field strength\n       </a>\n       , its on-orbit operational time at ISS is expected to be 10 to 18 years versus only three years for the superconducting version.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWST_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AWST-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In January 2014 it was announced that funding for the ISS had been extended until 2024.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1999, after the successful flight of AMS-01, the total cost of the AMS program was estimated to be $33 million, with AMS-02 planned for flight to the ISS in 2003.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       in 2003, and after a number of technical difficulties with the construction of AMS-02, the cost of the program ballooned to an estimated $2 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hsu_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hsu-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Installation_on_the_International_Space_Station">\n        Installation on the International Space Station\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Installation on the International Space Station">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:624px;max-width:624px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:251px;max-width:251px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AMS02onISS.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="3375" data-file-width="6000" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/AMS02onISS.jpg/249px-AMS02onISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/AMS02onISS.jpg/374px-AMS02onISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/AMS02onISS.jpg/498px-AMS02onISS.jpg 2x" width="249"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          A computer generated image showing AMS-02 mounted to the\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">\n           ISS\n          </a>\n          S3 Upper Inboard Payload Attach Site.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:369px;max-width:369px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="493" data-file-width="1112" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png/367px-ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png/551px-ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png/734px-ISS_Unpressurized_Platforms.png 2x" width="367"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Location of the AMS on the\n          <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n           International Space Station\n          </a>\n          (upper left).\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg/220px-STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg/330px-STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg/440px-STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-134_the_starboard_truss_of_the_ISS_with_the_newly-installed_AMS-02.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         AMS-02 installed on the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">\n          ISS\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For several years it was uncertain if AMS-02 would ever be launched because it was not manifested to fly on any of the remaining\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       flights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp-2007_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp-2007-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After the 2003\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       NASA decided to reduce shuttle flights and retire the remaining shuttles by 2010. A number of flights were removed from the remaining manifest including the flight for AMS-02.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2006 NASA studied alternative ways of delivering AMS-02 to the space station, but they all proved to be too expensive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp-2007_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp-2007-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In May 2008 a bill\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       was proposed to launch AMS-02 to ISS on an additional shuttle flight in 2010 or 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-House_Bill_Would_Authorize_Additional_Shuttle_Flights_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-House_Bill_Would_Authorize_Additional_Shuttle_Flights-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The bill was passed by the full\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       on 11 June 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The bill then went before the Senate Commerce, Science and Transportation Committee where it also passed. It was then amended and passed by the full\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       on 25 September 2008, and was passed again by the House on 27 September 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Congress_Passes_Final_Version_HR6063_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Congress_Passes_Final_Version_HR6063-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was signed by President\n       <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">\n        George W. Bush\n       </a>\n       on 15 October 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bush_Signs_NASA_Authorization_Act_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bush_Signs_NASA_Authorization_Act-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_-_H.R.6063_-_Major_Actions_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress_-_H.R.6063_-_Major_Actions-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The bill authorized NASA to add another space shuttle flight to the schedule before the space shuttle program was discontinued. In January 2009 NASA restored AMS-02 to the shuttle manifest. On 26 August 2010, AMS-02 was delivered from\n       <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">\n        CERN\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_C-5_Galaxy" title="Lockheed C-5 Galaxy">\n        Lockheed C-5 Galaxy\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It was delivered to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       on May 19, 2011 as part of station assembly flight\n       <b>\n        ULF6\n       </b>\n       on shuttle flight\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n        STS-134\n       </a>\n       , commanded by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_Kelly_(astronaut)" title="Mark Kelly (astronaut)">\n        Mark Kelly\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manifest_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-manifest-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was removed from the shuttle cargo bay using the shuttle\'s robotic arm and handed off to the station\'s robotic arm for installation. AMS-02 is mounted on top of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        Integrated Truss Structure\n       </a>\n       , on USS-02, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zenith" title="Zenith">\n        zenith\n       </a>\n       side of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure#P3.2FP4.2C_S3.2FS4_truss_assemblies" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        S3-element\n       </a>\n       of the truss.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-AMS-02_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-AMS-02-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">\n        Specifications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Specifications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Mass: 8,500\xc2\xa0kg\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Power: 2,500\xc2\xa0W\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Internal data rate: 7\xc2\xa0Gbit/s\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Data rate to ground: 2\xc2\xa0Mbit/s (typical, average)\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ams-facts-figures_38-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ams-facts-figures-38">\n          [38]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Primary mission duration: 10 to 18 years\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Magnetic field intensity: 0.15\n        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_(unit)" title="Tesla (unit)">\n         teslas\n        </a>\n        produced by a 1,200\xc2\xa0kg permanent\n        <a href="/wiki/Neodymium_magnet" title="Neodymium magnet">\n         neodymium magnet\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ams-facts-figures_38-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ams-facts-figures-38">\n          [38]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Original superconducting magnet: 2 coils of\n        <a href="/wiki/Niobium-titanium" title="Niobium-titanium">\n         niobium-titanium\n        </a>\n        at 1.8\xc2\xa0K producing a central field of 0.87\n        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_(unit)" title="Tesla (unit)">\n         teslas\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n         <a href="#cite_note-39">\n          [39]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        AMS-02 flight magnet changed to non-superconducting AMS-01 version to extend experiment life and to solve reliability problems in the operation of the superconducting system\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       About 1,000 cosmic rays are recorded by the instrument per second, generating about one\n       <a href="/wiki/Gigabyte" title="Gigabyte">\n        GB/sec\n       </a>\n       of data. This data is filtered and compressed to about 300 kB/sec for download to the operation center POCC at CERN.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">\n        Design\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Design">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The detector module consists of a series of detectors that are used to determine various characteristics of the radiation and particles as they pass through. Characteristics are determined only for particles that pass through from top to bottom. Particles that enter the detector at any other angles are rejected. From top to bottom the subsystems are identified as:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Transition_radiation_detector" title="Transition radiation detector">\n         Transition radiation detector\n        </a>\n        measures the velocities of the highest energy particles;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Upper time of flight counter, along with the lower time of flight counter, measures the velocities of lower energy particles;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Star tracker determines the orientation of the module in space;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Silicon tracker measures the coordinates of charged particles in the magnetic field;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Permanent magnet bends the path of charged particles so they can be identified;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Anti-coincidence counter rejects stray particles that enter through the sides;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ring_imaging_Cherenkov_detector" title="Ring imaging Cherenkov detector">\n         Ring imaging Cherenkov detector\n        </a>\n        measures velocity of fast particles with extreme accuracy;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Electromagnetic calorimeter measures the total energy of the particles.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_goals">\n        Scientific goals\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Scientific goals">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The AMS-02 will use the unique environment of space to advance knowledge of the Universe and lead to the understanding of its origin by searching for antimatter,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">\n        dark matter\n       </a>\n       and measuring\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">\n        cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-AMS-02_37-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-AMS-02-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Antimatter">\n        Antimatter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Antimatter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">\n        Antimatter\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Experimental evidence indicates that\n       <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">\n        our galaxy\n       </a>\n       is made of\n       <a href="/wiki/Matter" title="Matter">\n        matter\n       </a>\n       ; however, scientists believe there are about 100\xe2\x80\x93200 billion galaxies in the Universe and some versions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">\n        Big Bang\n       </a>\n       theory of the origin of the Universe require equal amounts of matter and antimatter. Theories that explain this apparent asymmetry violate other measurements. Whether or not there is significant antimatter is one of the fundamental questions of the origin and nature of the Universe. Any observations of an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antihelium" title="Antihelium">\n        antihelium\n       </a>\n       nucleus would provide evidence for the existence of antimatter in space. In 1999,\n       <i>\n        AMS-01\n       </i>\n       established a new upper limit of 10\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x926\n       </sup>\n       for the antihelium/helium flux ratio in the Universe. AMS-02 will search with a sensitivity of 10\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x929\n       </sup>\n       , an improvement of three orders of magnitude over\n       <i>\n        AMS-01\n       </i>\n       , sufficient to reach the edge of the expanding Universe and resolve the issue definitively.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_matter">\n        Dark matter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dark matter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">\n        Dark matter\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The visible matter in the Universe, such as stars, adds up to less than 5 percent of the total mass that is known to exist from many other observations. The other 95 percent is dark, either dark matter, which is estimated at 20 percent of the Universe by weight, or\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">\n        dark energy\n       </a>\n       , which makes up the balance. The exact nature of both still is unknown. One of the leading candidates for dark matter is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutralino" title="Neutralino">\n        neutralino\n       </a>\n       . If neutralinos exist, they should be colliding with each other and giving off an excess of charged particles that can be detected by AMS-02. Any peaks in the background\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positron\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Antiproton" title="Antiproton">\n        antiproton\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n        gamma ray\n       </a>\n       flux could signal the presence of neutralinos or other dark matter candidates, but would need to be distinguished from poorly known\n       <a href="/wiki/Confounding" title="Confounding">\n        confounding\n       </a>\n       astrophysical signals.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Strangelets">\n        Strangelets\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Strangelets">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Strangelet" title="Strangelet">\n        Strangelet\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Six types of\n       <a href="/wiki/Quark" title="Quark">\n        quarks\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Up_quark" title="Up quark">\n        up\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Down_quark" title="Down quark">\n        down\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Strange_quark" title="Strange quark">\n        strange\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Charm_quark" title="Charm quark">\n        charm\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bottom_quark" title="Bottom quark">\n        bottom\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Top_quark" title="Top quark">\n        top\n       </a>\n       ) have been found experimentally; however, the majority of matter on Earth is made up of only up and down quarks. It is a fundamental question whether there exists stable matter made up of strange quarks in combination with up and down quarks. Particles of such matter are known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Strangelet" title="Strangelet">\n        strangelets\n       </a>\n       . Strangelets might have extremely large mass and very small charge-to-mass ratios. It would be a totally new form of matter. AMS-02 may determine whether this extraordinary matter exists in our local environment.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_radiation_environment">\n        Space radiation environment\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Space radiation environment">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">\n        Cosmic radiation\n       </a>\n       during transit is a significant obstacle to\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_mission_to_Mars" title="Human mission to Mars">\n        sending humans to Mars\n       </a>\n       . Accurate measurements of the cosmic ray environment are needed to plan appropriate countermeasures. Most cosmic ray studies are done by balloon-borne instruments with flight times that are measured in days; these studies have shown significant variations. AMS-02 will be operative on the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       , gathering a large amount of accurate data and allowing measurements of the long term variation of the cosmic ray flux over a wide energy range, for nuclei from\n       <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">\n        protons\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">\n        iron\n       </a>\n       . In addition to the understanding the radiation protection required for astronauts during\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">\n        interplanetary flight\n       </a>\n       , this data will allow the interstellar propagation and origins of cosmic rays to be identified.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Results">\n        Results\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Results">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In July 2012, it was reported that AMS-02 had observed over 18 billion cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2012-07-25_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_2012-07-25-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In February 2013, Samuel Ting acknowledged that he would be publishing the first scholarly paper in a few weeks, and that in its first 18 months of operation AMS had recorded 25 billion particle events including nearly eight billion fast electrons and positrons.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2013-02-18_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_2013-02-18-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The AMS paper reported the positron-electron ratio in the mass range of 0.5 to 350\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GeV" title="GeV">\n        GeV\n       </a>\n       , providing evidence about the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weakly_interacting_massive_particle" title="Weakly interacting massive particle">\n        weakly interacting massive particle\n       </a>\n       (WIMP) model of dark matter.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 30 March 2013, the first results from the AMS experiment were announced by the\n       <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">\n        CERN\n       </a>\n       press office.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physrevltrs413_8-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-physrevltrs413-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMS-20130403_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AMS-20130403-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20130403_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20130403-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-20130403_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-20130403-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20130403_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20130403-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130403_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130403-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-First_result_from_the_AMS_experiment_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-First_result_from_the_AMS_experiment-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first physics results were published in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Physical_Review_Letters" title="Physical Review Letters">\n         Physical Review Letters\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       on 3 April 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physrevltrs413_8-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-physrevltrs413-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A total of 6.8\xc3\x9710\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positron\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">\n        electron\n       </a>\n       events were collected in the energy range from 0.5 to 350 GeV. The positron fraction (of the total electron plus positron events) steadily increased from energies of 10 to 250\xe2\x80\x89\xe2\x80\x89GeV, but the slope decreased by an order of magnitude above 20 GeV, even though the fraction of positrons still increased. There was no fine structure in the positron fraction spectrum, and no\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anisotropies" title="Anisotropies">\n        anisotropies\n       </a>\n       were observed. The accompanying\n       <i>\n        Physics\n       </i>\n       Viewpoint\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       said that "The first results from the space-borne Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer confirm an unexplained excess of high-energy positrons in Earth-bound cosmic rays." These results are consistent with the positrons originating from the annihilation of dark matter particles in space, but not yet sufficiently conclusive to rule out other explanations.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samuel_Ting" title="Samuel Ting">\n        Samuel Ting\n       </a>\n       said \xe2\x80\x9cOver the coming months, AMS will be able to tell us conclusively whether these positrons are a signal for dark matter, or whether they have some other origin."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On September 18, 2014, new results with almost twice as much data were presented in a talk at CERN and published in\n       <i>\n        Physical Review Letters\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A new measurement of positron fraction up to 500 GeV was reported, showing that positron fraction peaks at a maximum of about 16% of total electron+positron events, around an energy of 275 \xc2\xb1 32 GeV. At higher energies, up to 500 GeV, the ratio of positrons to electrons begins to fall again.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       AMS presented for 3 days at CERN in April 2015, covering new data on 300 million proton events and helium flux.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It revealed in December 2016 that it had discovered a few signals consistent with antihelium nuclei amidst several billion helium nuclei. The result remains to be verified, and the team is currently trying to rule out contamination.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" Observatories)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_for_Antimatter_Matter_Exploration_and_Light-nuclei_Astrophysics" title="Payload for Antimatter Matter Exploration and Light-nuclei Astrophysics">\n         Payload for Antimatter Matter Exploration and Light-nuclei Astrophysics\n        </a>\n        (PAMELA) \xe2\x80\x93 an Italian-international cosmic ray mission launched in 2006 with similar goals\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_research_on_the_ISS" title="Scientific research on the ISS">\n         Scientific research on the ISS\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span href="http://ams-02project.jsc.nasa.gov/html/Projectpage.htm" rel="nofollow">\n        "AMS project page"\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <ol class="references">\n        <li id="cite_note-launchslip2-1">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-launchslip2_1-0">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n
